class="external text" href="http://www.shell.com">www<wbr />.shell<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Royal Dutch Shell plc</b> (<a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">LSE</a>:&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.londonstockexchange.com/exchange/searchengine/search.html?lang=en&amp;x=0&amp;y=0&amp;q=RDSA">RDSA</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.londonstockexchange.com/exchange/prices-and-news/stocks/prices-search/stock-prices-search.html?nameCode=RDSB">RDSB</a>), commonly known  as <b>Shell</b>, is an Anglo-Dutch multinational <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">gas</a> company headquartered in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and incorporated in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Shell.com_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shell.com-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> It is one of the six oil and gas "<a href="/wiki/Supermajor" class="mw-redirect" title="Supermajor">supermajors</a>" and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_companies_by_revenue" title="List of largest companies by revenue">sixth-largest company in the world measured by 2016 revenues</a> (and the largest based in Europe).<sup id="cite_ref-results_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-results-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Shell was first in the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a> list of the world\'s largest companies;<sup id="cite_ref-fortune500_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune500-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> in that year its revenues were equivalent to 84% of the Netherlands\' $556 billion GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Shell is <a href="/wiki/Vertical_integration" title="Vertical integration">vertically integrated</a> and is active in every area of the oil and gas industry, including <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">exploration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extraction_of_petroleum" title="Extraction of petroleum">production</a>, <a href="/wiki/Refining" title="Refining">refining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_transport" title="Petroleum transport">transport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midstream" title="Midstream">distribution and marketing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">petrochemicals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Power_generation" class="mw-redirect" title="Power generation">power generation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trader_(finance)" title="Trader (finance)">trading</a>. It also has <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> activities, including in <a href="/wiki/Biofuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Biofuels">biofuels</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind</a><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and hydrogen.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Shell has operations in over 70 countries, produces around 3.7&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Barrel_of_oil_equivalent" title="Barrel of oil equivalent">barrels of oil equivalent</a> per day and has 44,000 service stations worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bgcombin_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bgcombin-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> As of 31 December 2014, Shell had total proved reserves of 13.7&#160;billion barrels (2.18<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\xc3\x97</span>10<sup>9</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of oil equivalent.<sup id="cite_ref-bgcombin_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bgcombin-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shell_Oil_Company" title="Shell Oil Company">Shell Oil Company</a>, its principal subsidiary in the United States, is one of its largest businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Shell holds 50% of <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%ADzen" title="Ra\xc3\xadzen">Ra\xc3\xadzen</a>, a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Cosan" title="Cosan">Cosan</a>, which is the third-largest Brazil-based energy company by revenues and a major producer of <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sugarcane_Ethanol_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sugarcane_Ethanol-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shell was formed in 1907 through the amalgamation of the Royal Dutch Petroleum Company of the Netherlands and the "Shell" Transport and Trading Company of the United Kingdom. Until its unification in 2005 the firm operated as a dual-listed company, whereby the British and Dutch companies maintained their legal existence but operated as a single-unit partnership for business purposes. Shell first entered the chemicals industry in 1929. In 1970 Shell acquired the mining company Billiton, which it subsequently sold in 1994 and now forms part of <a href="/wiki/BHP_Billiton" class="mw-redirect" title="BHP Billiton">BHP Billiton</a>. In recent decades gas exploration and production has become an increasingly important part of Shell\'s business.<sup id="cite_ref-bloom8415_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloom8415-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Shell acquired <a href="/wiki/BG_Group" title="BG Group">BG Group</a> in 2016, making it the world\'s largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_natural_gas" title="Liquefied natural gas">liquefied natural gas</a> (LNG).<sup id="cite_ref-bloom8415_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloom8415-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shell has a primary listing on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> and is a constituent of the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_100_Index" title="FTSE 100 Index">FTSE 100 Index</a>. It had a <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Market capitalisation">market capitalisation</a> of \xc2\xa3185&#160;billion at the close of trading on 30 December 2016, by far the largest of any company listed on the London Stock Exchange and <a href="/wiki/List_of_corporations_by_market_capitalization" class="mw-redirect" title="List of corporations by market capitalization">among the highest of any company in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> It has secondary listings on <a href="/wiki/Euronext" title="Euronext">Euronext Amsterdam</a> and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>. As of January 2013, Shell\'s largest shareholder was <a href="/wiki/Capital_Group_Companies" title="Capital Group Companies">Capital Research Global Investors</a> with 9.85% ahead of <a href="/wiki/BlackRock" title="BlackRock">BlackRock</a> in second with 6.89%.<sup id="cite_ref-upstream070912_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upstream070912-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Shell\'s logo, known as the "pecten", is one of the most familiar commercial symbols in the world.\n</p>\n<div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44"><a href="#Notes"><span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Afscheepsteiger_Tarakan_14_TMnr_10010382.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Afscheepsteiger_Tarakan_14_TMnr_10010382.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Afscheepsteiger_Tarakan_14_TMnr_10010382.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Afscheepsteiger_Tarakan_14_TMnr_10010382.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Afscheepsteiger_Tarakan_14_TMnr_10010382.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Afscheepsteiger_Tarakan_14_TMnr_10010382.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Afscheepsteiger_Tarakan_14_TMnr_10010382.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="444" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Afscheepsteiger_Tarakan_14_TMnr_10010382.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Royal Dutch Petroleum dock in the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KITLV_-_26871_-_Kleingrothe,_C.J._-_Medan_-_Burning_of_natural_gases_at_an_oil_drilling_site,_presumably_at_Pangkalan_Brandan,_East_Coast_of_Sumatra_-_circa_1905.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/KITLV_-_26871_-_Kleingrothe%2C_C.J._-_Medan_-_Burning_of_natural_gases_at_an_oil_drilling_site%2C_presumably_at_Pangkalan_Brandan%2C_East_Coast_of_Sumatra_-_circa_1905.tif/lossy-page1-220px-thumbnail.tif.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/KITLV_-_26871_-_Kleingrothe%2C_C.J._-_Medan_-_Burning_of_natural_gases_at_an_oil_drilling_site%2C_presumably_at_Pangkalan_Brandan%2C_East_Coast_of_Sumatra_-_circa_1905.tif/lossy-page1-330px-thumbnail.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/KITLV_-_26871_-_Kleingrothe%2C_C.J._-_Medan_-_Burning_of_natural_gases_at_an_oil_drilling_site%2C_presumably_at_Pangkalan_Brandan%2C_East_Coast_of_Sumatra_-_circa_1905.tif/lossy-page1-440px-thumbnail.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2651" data-file-height="1608" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KITLV_-_26871_-_Kleingrothe,_C.J._-_Medan_-_Burning_of_natural_gases_at_an_oil_drilling_site,_presumably_at_Pangkalan_Brandan,_East_Coast_of_Sumatra_-_circa_1905.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The oil well at <a href="/wiki/Pangkalan_Brandan" title="Pangkalan Brandan">Pangkalan Brandan</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Sumatra" title="North Sumatra">North Sumatra</a> is considered to be the origin of the Royal Dutch Shell.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Royal Dutch Shell Group was created in April 1907 through the amalgamation of two rival companies: the Royal Dutch Petroleum Company (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Koninklijke Nederlandse Petroleum Maatschappij</i>) of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and the Shell Transport and Trading Company Limited of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-beginnings_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beginnings-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> It was a move largely driven by the need to compete globally with <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Aftalion2001_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aftalion2001-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The Royal Dutch Petroleum Company was a Dutch company founded in 1890 to develop an oilfield in <a href="/wiki/Pangkalan_Brandan" title="Pangkalan Brandan">Pangkalan Brandan</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Sumatra" title="North Sumatra">North Sumatra</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMerrillees201560_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMerrillees201560-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and initially led by <a href="/wiki/Jean_Baptiste_August_Kessler" title="Jean Baptiste August Kessler">August Kessler</a>, Hugo Loudon, and <a href="/wiki/Henri_Deterding" title="Henri Deterding">Henri Deterding</a>. The "Shell" Transport and Trading Company (the quotation marks were part of the legal name) was a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">British</a> company, founded in 1897 by <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Samuel,_1st_Viscount_Bearsted" title="Marcus Samuel, 1st Viscount Bearsted">Marcus Samuel</a>, 1st Viscount Bearsted, and his brother <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Samuel" title="Samuel Samuel">Samuel Samuel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Their father had owned an antique company in <a href="/wiki/Houndsditch" title="Houndsditch">Houndsditch</a>, London,<sup id="cite_ref-Forsyth2011_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forsyth2011-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> which expanded in 1833 to import and sell seashells, after which the company "Shell" took its name.<sup id="cite_ref-beginnings_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beginnings-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Falola_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Falola-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For various reasons, the new firm operated as a <a href="/wiki/Dual-listed_company" title="Dual-listed company">dual-listed company</a>, whereby the merging companies maintained their legal existence, but operated as a single-unit partnership for business purposes. The terms of the merger gave 60 percent ownership of the new group to the Dutch arm and 40 percent to the British.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerretson346_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerretson346-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>National patriotic sensibilities would not permit a full-scale merger or takeover of either of the two companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerretson346_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerretson346-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The Dutch company, <i>Koninklijke Nederlandsche Petroleum Maatschappij</i> at <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, was in charge of production and manufacture.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerretson347_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerretson347-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The British <i>Anglo-Saxon Petroleum Company</i> was based in London, to direct the transport and storage of the products.<sup id="cite_ref-Gerretson347_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerretson347-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aurora_1914_Sydney_Harbour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Aurora_1914_Sydney_Harbour.jpg/220px-Aurora_1914_Sydney_Harbour.jpg" width="220" height="289" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Aurora_1914_Sydney_Harbour.jpg/330px-Aurora_1914_Sydney_Harbour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Aurora_1914_Sydney_Harbour.jpg/440px-Aurora_1914_Sydney_Harbour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2818" data-file-height="3700" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aurora_1914_Sydney_Harbour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shell benzine for Sir Ernest Henry Shackleton, Antarctic Expedition 1915.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Shell_Fuel_Lkw_IMG_20180417_192801.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Ford_Shell_Fuel_Lkw_IMG_20180417_192801.jpg/220px-Ford_Shell_Fuel_Lkw_IMG_20180417_192801.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Ford_Shell_Fuel_Lkw_IMG_20180417_192801.jpg/330px-Ford_Shell_Fuel_Lkw_IMG_20180417_192801.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Ford_Shell_Fuel_Lkw_IMG_20180417_192801.jpg/440px-Ford_Shell_Fuel_Lkw_IMG_20180417_192801.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3045" data-file-height="2283" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Shell_Fuel_Lkw_IMG_20180417_192801.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shell tank truck from 1926 based on a <a href="/wiki/Ford_Model_TT" title="Ford Model TT">Ford Model TT</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shell_petrol_pump_1952.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Shell_petrol_pump_1952.jpg/220px-Shell_petrol_pump_1952.jpg" width="220" height="398" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Shell_petrol_pump_1952.jpg/330px-Shell_petrol_pump_1952.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Shell_petrol_pump_1952.jpg/440px-Shell_petrol_pump_1952.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1837" data-file-height="3326" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shell_petrol_pump_1952.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vintage petrol pump (1952)</div></div></div>\n<p>During the First World War, Shell was the main supplier of fuel to the <a href="/wiki/British_Expeditionary_Force_(World_War_I)" title="British Expeditionary Force (World War I)">British Expeditionary Force</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> It was also the sole supplier of aviation fuel and supplied 80 percent of the British Army\'s <a href="/wiki/TNT" title="TNT">TNT</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> It also volunteered all of its shipping to the British <a href="/wiki/Admiralty" title="Admiralty">Admiralty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The German invasion of Romania in 1916 saw 17% of the group\'s worldwide production destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1919, Shell took control of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Eagle_Petroleum_Company" title="Mexican Eagle Petroleum Company">Mexican Eagle Petroleum Company</a> and in 1921 formed Shell-Mex Limited which marketed products under the "Shell" and "Eagle" brands in the United Kingdom. In 1929, <a href="/wiki/Shell_Chemicals" title="Shell Chemicals">Shell Chemicals</a> was founded.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the 1920s, Shell was the world\'s leading oil company, producing 11 percent of the world\'s <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a> supply and owning 10 percent of its tanker tonnage.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_25-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Shell_Mex_House" title="Shell Mex House">Shell Mex House</a> was completed in 1931, and was the head office for Shell\'s marketing activity worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_25-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In 1932, partly in response to the difficult economic conditions of the times, Shell-Mex merged its UK marketing operations with those of <a href="/wiki/British_Petroleum" class="mw-redirect" title="British Petroleum">British Petroleum</a> to create <a href="/wiki/Shell-Mex_and_BP" title="Shell-Mex and BP">Shell-Mex and BP</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> a company that traded until the brands separated in 1975. Royal Dutch Company ranked 79th among United States corporations in the value of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> military production contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 1930s saw Shell\'s Mexican assets seized by the local government.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_25-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> After the invasion of the Netherlands by Germany in 1940, the head office of the Dutch companies was moved to <a href="/wiki/Curacao" class="mw-redirect" title="Curacao">Curacao</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_25-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In 1945 Shell\'s Danish headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, at the time being used by the <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">Gestapo</a>, was bombed by Royal Air Force <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Mosquito" title="De Havilland Mosquito">Mosquitoes</a> in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Carthage" title="Operation Carthage">Operation Carthage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Around 1952, Shell was the first company to purchase and use a computer in the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The computer, a <a href="/wiki/Ferranti_Mark_1" title="Ferranti Mark 1">Ferranti Mark 1*</a>, was assembled and used at the Shell laboratory in Amsterdam. In 1970 Shell acquired the mining company Billiton, which it subsequently sold in 1994 and now forms part of <a href="/wiki/BHP_Billiton" class="mw-redirect" title="BHP Billiton">BHP Billiton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In November 2004, following a period of turmoil caused by the revelation that Shell had been overstating its <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">oil reserves</a>, it was announced that the Shell Group would move to a single capital structure, creating a new parent company to be named Royal Dutch Shell plc, with its primary listing on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a>, a secondary listing on the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a>, its headquarters and tax residency in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, Netherlands and its registered office in London. The unification was completed on 20 July 2005 and the original owners delisted their companies from the respective exchanges. On 20 July 2005, the Shell Transport &amp; Trading Company plc was delisted from the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">LSE</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> where as, Royal Dutch Petroleum Company from <a href="/wiki/NYSE" class="mw-redirect" title="NYSE">NYSE</a> on 18 November 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The shares of the company were issued at a 60/40 advantage for the shareholders of Royal Dutch in line with the original ownership of the Shell Group.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Iraq#2009_Oil_services_contracts" title="Economy of Iraq">2009 Iraqi oil services contracts tender</a>, a consortium led by Shell (45%) and which included <a href="/wiki/Petronas" title="Petronas">Petronas</a> (30%) was awarded a production contract for the "Majnoon field" in the south of Iraq, which contains an estimated 12.6 billion barrels (2.00<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\xc3\x97</span>10<sup>9</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of oil.<sup id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-2009-47_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-2009-47-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The "West Qurna 1 field" production contract was awarded to a consortium led by <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a> (60%) and included Shell (15%).<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2010 Shell and <a href="/wiki/Cosan" title="Cosan">Cosan</a> formed a 50:50 joint-venture, <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%ADzen" title="Ra\xc3\xadzen">Ra\xc3\xadzen</a>, comprising all of Cosan\'s Brazilian ethanol, energy generation, fuel distribution and sugar activities, and all of Shell\'s Brazilian retail fuel and aviation distribution businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In March 2010, Shell announced the sale of some of its assets, including its liquefied petroleum gas (LPG) business, to meet the cost of a planned $28bn capital spending programme. Shell invited buyers to submit indicative bids, due by 22 March, with a plan to raise $2\xe2\x80\x933bn from the sale.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In June 2010, Royal Dutch Shell agreed to acquire all the business of East Resources for a cash consideration of $4.7&#160;billion. The transaction included East Resources\' tight gas fields.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Over the course of 2013, the corporation began the sale of its US shale gas assets and cancelled a US$20 billion gas project that was to be constructed in the US state of <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>. A new CEO Ben van Beurden was appointed in January 2014, prior to the announcement that the corporation\'s overall performance in 2013 was 38 per cent lower than 2012\xe2\x80\x94the value of Shell\'s shares fell by 3 per cent as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-Tom_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tom-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Following the sale of the majority of its Australian assets in February 2014, the corporation plans to sell a further US$15 billion worth of assets in the period leading up to 2015, with deals announced in Australia, Brazil and Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloom_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloom-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Royal Dutch Shell announced on 8 April 2015 it had agreed to buy <a href="/wiki/BG_Group" title="BG Group">BG Group</a> for \xc2\xa347&#160;billion (US$70&#160;billion), subject to shareholder and regulatory approval.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in February 2016, resulting in Shell surpassing <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron Corporation</a> and becoming the world\'s second largest non-state oil company.<sup id="cite_ref-Katakey_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Katakey-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 7 June 2016, Royal Dutch Shell announced that it would build an <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Shell_ethane_cracker_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Pennsylvania Shell ethane cracker plant">ethane cracker plant</a> near <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> after spending several years doing environmental cleanup of the proposed plant\'s site.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2017, Royal Dutch Shell agreed to sell \xc2\xa32.46bn worth of <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> assets to oil exploration firm <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chrysaor_(Oil_Exploration_firm)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chrysaor (Oil Exploration firm) (page does not exist)">Chrysaor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>  In 2017, Shell sold its <a href="/wiki/Oil_sands" title="Oil sands">oil sands</a> assets to <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Natural_Resources" title="Canadian Natural Resources">Canadian Natural Resources</a> in exchange of approximately 8.8% stake in that company. In May 2017, it was reported that Shell plans to sell its shares in Canadian Natural Resources fully exiting the oil sands business.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters240517_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters240517-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Environmental record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The presence of companies like Shell in the <a href="/wiki/Niger_Delta" title="Niger Delta">Niger-Delta</a> has led to extreme <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_the_Niger_Delta" title="Environmental issues in the Niger Delta">environmental issues in the Niger Delta</a>. Many pipelines in the Niger-Delta owned by Shell are old and corroded. Shell has acknowledged its responsibility for keeping the pipelines new but has also denied responsibility for environmental causes.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> This has led to mass protests from the Niger-Delta inhabitants, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Friends_of_the_Earth" title="Friends of the Earth">Friends of the Earth</a> Netherlands against Shell. It has also led to action plans to boycott Shell by environmental groups, and human rights groups.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In January 2013, a Dutch court rejected four out of five allegations brought against the firm over oil pollution in the Niger Delta but found a subsidiary guilty of one case of pollution, ordering compensation to be paid to a Nigerian farmer.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 15 January 1999, off the Argentinian town of <a href="/wiki/Magdalena,_Buenos_Aires" title="Magdalena, Buenos Aires">Magdalena, Buenos Aires</a>, the Shell tanker Estrella Pampeana collided with a German <a href="/wiki/Cargo_ship" title="Cargo ship">freighter</a>, emptying its contents into the lake, polluting the environment, drinkable water, plants and animals. Over a decade after the spill, a referendum held in Magdalena determined the acceptance of a US$9.5 million compensatory payout from Shell.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Shell denied responsibility for the spill, but an Argentine court ruled in 2002 that the corporation was responsible.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shell joined the <a href="/wiki/Global_Climate_Coalition" title="Global Climate Coalition">Global Climate Coalition</a> of businesses opposed to greenhouse gas emission regulation. In 1989, Shell redesigned a $3-billion North Sea natural gas platform in the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>, raising its height one to two meters, to accommodate an anticipated sea level rise due to global warming.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, Royal Dutch Shell PLC reported CO2 emissions of 81 million metric tonnes.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shell is known to be processing oil from the Amazon region of South America, a large concern for environmentalists trying to protect the area. In the United States, the Martinez refinery (CA) and the Puget Sound Refinery (WA) carry Amazonian oil. In 2015, 14% of the Martinez refinery\'s gross, at 19,570 barrels per day, came from the Amazon. <sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2017, a public information film unseen for years resurfaced and showed Shell had clear grasp of global warming 26 years earlier but has not acted accordingly since, said critics. <sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jelmer_Mommers_Damian_Carrington_2017_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jelmer_Mommers_Damian_Carrington_2017-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jelmer_Mommers_2017_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jelmer_Mommers_2017-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 4 August 2005, the board of directors announced the appointment of <a href="/wiki/Jorma_Ollila" title="Jorma Ollila">Jorma Ollila</a>, chairman and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a> at the time, to succeed Aad Jacobs as the company\'s non-executive chairman on 1 June 2006. Ollila is the first Shell chairman to be neither Dutch nor British. Other non-executive directors include <a href="/wiki/Maarten_van_den_Bergh" title="Maarten van den Bergh">Maarten van den Bergh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wim_Kok" title="Wim Kok">Wim Kok</a>, Nina Henderson, <a href="/wiki/John_Kerr,_Baron_Kerr_of_Kinlochard" title="John Kerr, Baron Kerr of Kinlochard">Lord Kerr</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Adelbert_van_Roxe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Adelbert van Roxe (page does not exist)">Adelbert van Roxe</a>, and Christine Morin-Postel.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 3 January 2014, <a href="/wiki/Ben_van_Beurden" title="Ben van Beurden">Ben van Beurden</a> is CEO of Shell.<sup id="cite_ref-Tom_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tom-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> His Predecessor was <a href="/wiki/Peter_Voser" title="Peter Voser">Peter Voser</a> who became CEO of Shell on 1 July 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Following a career at the corporation, in locations such as Australia and Africa, Ann Pickard was appointed as the executive vice president of the Arctic at Royal Dutch Shell, a role that was publicized in an interview with <a href="/wiki/McKinsey_%26_Company" title="McKinsey &amp; Company">McKinsey &amp; Company</a> in June 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Ann_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ann-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Name_and_logo">Name and logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Name and logo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The name Shell is linked to The "Shell" Transport and Trading Company.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In 1833, the founder\'s father, Marcus Samuel Sr., founded an import business to sell <a href="/wiki/Seashell" title="Seashell">seashells</a> to London collectors. When collecting seashell <a href="/wiki/Biological_specimen" title="Biological specimen">specimens</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> area in 1892, the younger Samuel realised there was potential in exporting <a href="/wiki/Oil_lamp" title="Oil lamp">lamp oil</a> from the region and commissioned the world\'s first purpose-built <a href="/wiki/Oil_tanker" title="Oil tanker">oil tanker</a>, the <a href="/wiki/SS_Murex_(1892)" title="SS Murex (1892)"><i>Murex</i></a> (Latin for a type of <a href="/wiki/Murex" title="Murex">snail shell</a>), to enter this market; by 1907 the company had a fleet. Although for several decades the company had a refinery at <a href="/wiki/Shell_Haven" title="Shell Haven">Shell Haven</a> on the Thames, there is no evidence of this having provided the name.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Shell logo is one of the most familiar commercial symbols in the world. This logo is known as the "<a href="/wiki/Pecten_(bivalve)" title="Pecten (bivalve)">pecten</a>" after the sea shell <i><a href="/wiki/Pecten_maximus" title="Pecten maximus">Pecten maximus</a></i> (the giant <a href="/wiki/Scallop" title="Scallop">scallop</a>), on which its design is based. The yellow and red colours used are thought<sup id="cite_ref-Superbrands_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Superbrands-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> to relate to the colours of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Spain" title="Flag of Spain">flag of Spain</a>, as Shell built early service stations in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, previously a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish colony</a>. The current revision of the logo was designed by <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Loewy" title="Raymond Loewy">Raymond Loewy</a> in 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The slash was removed from the name "Royal Dutch/Shell" in 2005, concurrent with moves to merge the two legally separate companies (Royal Dutch and Shell) to the single legal entity which exists today.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo_evolution">Logo evolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Logo evolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width:
