class="gallerytext">\n<p>1930\xe2\x80\x931971\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:19.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shell_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e8/Shell_logo.svg/120px-Shell_logo.svg.png" width="120" height="111" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e8/Shell_logo.svg/180px-Shell_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e8/Shell_logo.svg/240px-Shell_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="136" data-file-height="126" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>1971\xe2\x80\x93present\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_groupings">Business groupings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Business groupings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oil_platform.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Oil_platform.jpeg/220px-Oil_platform.jpeg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Oil_platform.jpeg/330px-Oil_platform.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Oil_platform.jpeg/440px-Oil_platform.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oil_platform.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Upstream_(oil_industry)" class="mw-redirect" title="Upstream (oil industry)">Upstream</a> activities currently generate around two-thirds of Shell\'s revenues</div></div></div>\n<p>Shell is currently organised into four major business groupings:<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Upstream</b>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 manages the upstream business. It searches for and recovers crude oil and natural gas and operates the upstream and midstream infrastructure necessary to deliver oil and gas to the market. Its activities are organised primarily within geographic units, although there are some activities that are managed across the business or provided through support units.</li>\n<li><b>Integrated Gas and New Energies</b>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 manages liquefying natural gas, converting gas to liquids and low-carbon opportunities.</li>\n<li><b>Downstream</b>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 manages Shell\'s manufacturing, distribution and marketing activities for oil products and chemicals. Manufacturing and supply includes refinery, supply and shipping of crude oil.</li>\n<li><b>Projects and technology</b>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 manages the delivery of Shell\'s major projects, provides technical services and technology capability covering both upstream and downstream activities. It is also responsible for providing functional leadership across Shell in the areas of health, safety and environment, and contracting and procurement.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_and_gas_activities">Oil and gas activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Oil and gas activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HK_Shell_depot.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/HK_Shell_depot.JPG/220px-HK_Shell_depot.JPG" width="220" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/HK_Shell_depot.JPG/330px-HK_Shell_depot.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/HK_Shell_depot.JPG/440px-HK_Shell_depot.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2041" data-file-height="2881" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HK_Shell_depot.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former Shell oil depot in <a href="/wiki/Kowloon" title="Kowloon">Kowloon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> around the mid-1980s</div></div></div>\n<p>Shell\'s primary business is the management of a <a href="/wiki/Vertical_integration" title="Vertical integration">vertically integrated</a> oil company. The development of technical and commercial expertise in all stages of this vertical integration, from the initial search for oil (exploration) through its harvesting (production), transportation, <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">refining</a> and finally trading and marketing established the core competencies on which the company was founded. Similar competencies were required for natural gas, which has become one of the most important businesses in which Shell is involved, and which contributes a significant proportion of the company\'s profits. While the vertically integrated business model provided significant <a href="/wiki/Economies_of_scale" title="Economies of scale">economies of scale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barriers_to_entry" title="Barriers to entry">barriers to entry</a>, each business now seeks to be a self-supporting unit without subsidies from other parts of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Traditionally, Shell was a heavily decentralised business worldwide (especially in the downstream) with companies in over 100 countries, each of which operated with a high degree of independence. The upstream tended to be far more centralised with much of the technical and financial direction coming from the central offices in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>. The upstream oil sector is also commonly known as the "exploration and production" sector.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Downstream operations, which now also includes the chemicals business, generates a third of Shell\'s profits worldwide and is known for its global network of more than 40,000 <a href="/wiki/Petrol_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Petrol station">petrol stations</a> and its various <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refineries</a>. The downstream business, which in some countries also included <a href="/wiki/Oil_refining" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil refining">oil refining</a>, generally included a retail <a href="/wiki/Petrol_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Petrol station">petrol station</a> network, lubricants manufacture and marketing, industrial fuel and lubricants sales and a host of other product/market sectors such as <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_petroleum_gas" title="Liquefied petroleum gas">LPG</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bitumen" class="mw-redirect" title="Bitumen">bitumen</a>. The practice in Shell was that these businesses were essentially local and that they were best managed by local "operating companies"&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 often with middle and senior management reinforced by <a href="/wiki/Expatriates" class="mw-redirect" title="Expatriates">expatriates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorships">Sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sponsorships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Shell has a long history of motorsport sponsorship, most notably <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Scuderia Ferrari</a> (1951-1964, 1966-1973 and 1996-present), <a href="/wiki/BRM" class="mw-redirect" title="BRM">BRM</a> (1962-1966 and 1968-1972), <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Toro_Rosso" title="Scuderia Toro Rosso">Scuderia Toro Rosso</a> (2007-2013 and 2016), <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a> (1967-1968 and 1984-1994), <a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus" title="Team Lotus">Lotus</a> (1968-1971), <a href="/wiki/Team_Penske" title="Team Penske">Team Penske</a> (2011\xe2\x80\x93present), <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motorsport" title="Hyundai Motorsport">Hyundai Motorsport</a> (since 2005), <a href="/wiki/AF_Corse" title="AF Corse">AF Corse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Risi_Competizione" title="Risi Competizione">Risi Competizione</a>, <a href="/wiki/BMW_Motorsport" title="BMW Motorsport">BMW Motorsport</a> (2015-present with also <a href="/wiki/Pennzoil" title="Pennzoil">Pennzoil</a>) and <a href="/wiki/DJR_Team_Penske" title="DJR Team Penske">Dick Johnson Racing</a> (<a href="/wiki/1987_Australian_Touring_Car_Championship" title="1987 Australian Touring Car Championship">1987</a>-<a href="/wiki/2004_V8_Supercar_Championship_Series" title="2004 V8 Supercar Championship Series">2004</a>). It will again become title sponsor for the latter (now rebranded as <a href="/wiki/DJR_Team_Penske" title="DJR Team Penske">DJR Team Penske</a>) in <a href="/wiki/2017_International_V8_Supercars_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="2017 International V8 Supercars Championship">2017</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Shell began drilling for oil in Africa during the 1950s. Shell began production in <a href="/wiki/Shell_Nigeria" title="Shell Nigeria">Nigeria</a> in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Shell operates in the <a href="/wiki/Upstream_(petroleum_industry)" title="Upstream (petroleum industry)">upstream oil sector</a> in Algeria, Cameroon, Egypt, Gabon where is the giant Rabi-Kounga oil field, Ghana, Libya, Morocco, Nigeria, South Africa and Tunisia; and in the <a href="/wiki/Downstream_(petroleum_industry)" title="Downstream (petroleum industry)">downstream sector</a> in 16 other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, Shell told US diplomats that it had placed staff in all the main ministries of the government.<sup id="cite_ref-grip_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grip-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2010, Shell announced its intention to <a href="/wiki/Divestment" title="Divestment">divest</a> from downstream business of all African countries except South Africa and Egypt to <a href="/wiki/Vitol" title="Vitol">Vitol</a> and "Helios".<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In several countries such as Tunisia, protests and strikes broke out. Shell denied rumours of the sellout.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Shell continues however upstream activities/extracting crude oil in the oil-rich <a href="/wiki/Niger_Delta" title="Niger Delta">Niger Delta</a> as well as downstream/commercial activities in South Africa. In June 2013, the company announced a strategic review of its operations in Nigeria, hinting that assets could be divested. In August 2014, the company disclosed it was in the process of finalizing the sale of its interests in four Nigerian oil fields.<sup id="cite_ref-ShellNigeria_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShellNigeria-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandakan_Sabah_Shell-Station-Labuk_Road-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Sandakan_Sabah_Shell-Station-Labuk_Road-01.jpg/220px-Sandakan_Sabah_Shell-Station-Labuk_Road-01.jpg" width="220" height="106" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Sandakan_Sabah_Shell-Station-Labuk_Road-01.jpg/330px-Sandakan_Sabah_Shell-Station-Labuk_Road-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Sandakan_Sabah_Shell-Station-Labuk_Road-01.jpg/440px-Sandakan_Sabah_Shell-Station-Labuk_Road-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5544" data-file-height="2678" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandakan_Sabah_Shell-Station-Labuk_Road-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Shell gasoline station in <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The company has upstream operations in unconventional oil and gas in China. Shell has a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/PetroChina" title="PetroChina">PetroChina</a> at the Changbei <a href="/wiki/Tight_gas" title="Tight gas">tight gas</a> field in <a href="/wiki/Shaanxi" title="Shaanxi">Shaanxi</a>, which has produced natural gas since 2008. The company has also invested in exploring for shale oil in Sichuan.<sup id="cite_ref-tightgas_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tightgas-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The other unconventional resource which Shell invested in in China was shale. The company was an early entrant in shale oil exploration in China but scaled down operations in 2014 due to difficulties with geology and population density.<sup id="cite_ref-shale_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shale-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> It has a joint venture to explore for <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale" title="Oil shale">oil shale</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jilin" title="Jilin">Jilin</a> through a joint venture with Jilin Guangzheng Mineral Development Company Limited.<sup id="cite_ref-shell_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shell-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hong_Kong">Hong Kong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hong Kong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Shell has been active in Hong Kong for a century, providing Retail, LPG, Commercial Fuel, Lubricants, Bitumen, Aviation, Marine and Chemicals services and products. Shell also sponsored the first Hong Kong-built aircraft, Inspiration\', for its around-the-world trip.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Malaysia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Shell discovered the first oil well in Malaysia in 1910, in <a href="/wiki/Miri,_Malaysia" title="Miri, Malaysia">Miri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a>. Today the oil well is a state monument known as the Grand Old Lady. In 1914, following this discovery, Shell built Malaysia\'s first oil refinery and laid a submarine pipeline in Miri.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ShellPhiljf539.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/ShellPhiljf539.JPG/220px-ShellPhiljf539.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/ShellPhiljf539.JPG/330px-ShellPhiljf539.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/ShellPhiljf539.JPG/440px-ShellPhiljf539.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ShellPhiljf539.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shell oil depot (Poro Point, <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando,_La_Union" title="San Fernando, La Union">San Fernando, La Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>).</div></div></div>\n<p>Royal Dutch Shell operates in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> under its subsidiary, <b>Pilipinas Shell Petroleum Corporation</b>. Its headquarters is in <a href="/wiki/Makati" title="Makati">Makati City</a> and it has facilities in the <a href="/wiki/Pandacan,_Manila#From_industrial_to_commercial" class="mw-redirect" title="Pandacan, Manila">Pandacan oil depot</a> and other key locations.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On January 2010, the Bureau of Customs claimed 7.34&#160;billion pesos worth of unpaid <a href="/wiki/Excise_taxes" class="mw-redirect" title="Excise taxes">excise taxes</a> against <i>Pilipinas Shell</i> for importing Catalytic cracked gasoline (CCG) and light catalytic cracked gasoline (LCCG) stating that those imports are bound for tariff charges.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2016, Pilipinas Shell filed an application to sell US$629 million worth of primary and secondary shares to the investing public (registration statement) with the SEC.  This was a prelude to filing its IPO listing application with the Philippine Stock Exchange.  On 3 November 2016 the Pilipinas Shell Petroleum Corporation was officially listed on the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Stock_Exchange" title="Philippine Stock Exchange">Philippine Stock Exchange</a> under the ticker symbol SHLPH after they held its <a href="/wiki/Initial_Public_Offering" class="mw-redirect" title="Initial Public Offering">Initial Public Offering</a> on 19 to 25 October of the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Singapore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Shell has a strong presence in Singapore, indeed Singapore is the main centre for Shell\'s petrochemical operations in Asia Pacific region. Shell Eastern Petroleum limited (SEPL) have their refinery located in Singapore\'s Pulau Bukom island. They also operate as Shell Chemicals Seraya in Jurong Island.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Shell first started trading in Ireland in 1902.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Shell E&amp;P Ireland (SEPIL) (previously Enterprise Energy Ireland) is an Irish exploration and production subsidiary of Royal Dutch Shell. Its headquarters are on <a href="/wiki/Leeson_Street" title="Leeson Street">Leeson Street</a> in Dublin. It was acquired in May 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Its main project is the <a href="/wiki/Corrib_gas_project" title="Corrib gas project">Corrib gas project</a>, a large gas field off the northwest coast, for which Shell has encountered <a href="/wiki/Corrib_gas_controversy" title="Corrib gas controversy">controversy and protests</a> in relation to the onshore pipeline and licence terms.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2005 Shell disposed of its entire retail and commercial fuels business in Ireland to <a href="/wiki/Topaz_Energy" title="Topaz Energy">Topaz Energy</a> Group. This included depots, company-owned petrol stations and supply agreements stations throughout the island of Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The retail outlets were re-branded as Topaz in 2008/9.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nordic_countries">Nordic countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Nordic countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 27 August 2007, Royal Dutch Shell and <a href="/wiki/Reitan_Group" title="Reitan Group">Reitan Group</a>, the owner of the <a href="/wiki/7-Eleven" title="7-Eleven">7-Eleven</a> brand in Scandinavia, announced an agreement to re-brand some 269 service stations across Norway, Sweden, Finland and Denmark, subject to obtaining regulatory approvals under the different competition laws in each country.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> On April 2010 Shell announced that the corporation is in process of trying to find a potential buyer for all of its operations in Finland and is doing similar market research concerning Swedish operations.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> On October 2010 Shell\'s gas stations and the heavy vehicle fuel supply networks in Finland and Sweden, along with a refinery located in <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a>, Sweden were sold to <a href="/wiki/St1" title="St1">St1</a>, a Finnish energy company, more precisely to its major shareholding parent company Keele Oy.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the UK sector of the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> Shell employs around 4,500 staff in Scotland as well as an additional 1,000 service contractors: however in August 2014 it announced it was laying off 250 of them, mainly in <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ShellUK_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShellUK-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Shell_Oil_Company" title="Shell Oil Company">Shell Oil Company</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shell_Canada" title="Shell Canada">Shell Canada</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shellgasstationlosthills.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Shellgasstationlosthills.jpg/220px-Shellgasstationlosthills.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Shellgasstationlosthills.jpg/330px-Shellgasstationlosthills.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Shellgasstationlosthills.jpg/440px-Shellgasstationlosthills.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1234" data-file-height="792" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shellgasstationlosthills.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Filling_station" title="Filling station">Service station</a> near <a href="/wiki/Lost_Hills,_California" title="Lost Hills, California">Lost Hills, California</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shell_gas_sign.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Shell_gas_sign.JPG/220px-Shell_gas_sign.JPG" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Shell_gas_sign.JPG/330px-Shell_gas_sign.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Shell_gas_sign.JPG/440px-Shell_gas_sign.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shell_gas_sign.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shell <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a> station sign in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CanadaShellStation4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/CanadaShellStation4.jpg/220px-CanadaShellStation4.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/CanadaShellStation4.jpg/330px-CanadaShellStation4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/CanadaShellStation4.jpg/440px-CanadaShellStation4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4573" data-file-height="3048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CanadaShellStation4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shell gasoline station in Canada</div></div></div>\n<p>Through most of Shell\'s early history, the <a href="/wiki/Shell_Oil_Company" title="Shell Oil Company">Shell Oil Company</a> business in the United States was substantially independent. Its stock was traded on the <a href="/wiki/NYSE" class="mw-redirect" title="NYSE">NYSE</a>, and the group\'s central office had little direct involvement in running the operation. However, in 1984, Royal Dutch Shell made a bid to purchase those shares of Shell Oil Company it did not own (around 30%) and, despite opposition from some minority shareholders which led to a court case, Shell completed the buyout for a sum of $5.7&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-hayes_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hayes-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>On 20 May 2011, Royal Dutch Shell\'s final investment decision for the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Floating_liquefied_natural_gas" title="Floating liquefied natural gas">floating liquefied natural gas</a> (FLNG) facility was finalized following the discovery of the remote offshore Prelude field\xe2\x80\x94located off Australia\'s northwestern coast and estimated to contain about 3 trillion cubic feet of natural gas equivalent reserves\xe2\x80\x94in 2007. FLNG technology is based on liquefied natural gas (LNG) developments that were pioneered in the mid-20th century and facilitates the exploitation of untapped natural gas reserves located in remote areas, often too small to extract any other way.<sup id="cite_ref-Post_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Post-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pete_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pete-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Shell_floating_LNG_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Shell floating LNG plant">floating vessel</a> to be used for the Prelude field, known as <a href="/wiki/Prelude_FLNG" title="Prelude FLNG"><i>Prelude</i> FLNG</a>, is promoted as the longest floating structure in the world and will take in the equivalent of 110,000 barrels of oil per day in natural gas\xe2\x80\x94at a location 200&#160;km (125 miles) off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>\xe2\x80\x94and cool it into liquefied natural gas for transport and sale in Asia. The Prelude is expected to start producing LNG in 2017<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94analysts estimated the total cost of construction at more than <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$12 billion</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Post_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Post-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pete_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pete-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the decision by the Royal Dutch Shell fuel corporation to close its <a href="/wiki/Geelong" title="Geelong">Geelong</a>, Australia refinery in April 2013, a third consecutive annual loss was recorded for Shell\'s Australian refining and fuel marketing assets. Revealed in June 2013, the writedown is worth <a href="/wiki/Australian_dollar" title="Australian dollar">A$</a>203 million, and was preceded by a A$638m writedown in 2012 and a A$407m writedown in 2011, after the closure of the Clyde refinery in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2014, Shell sold its Australian refinery and petrol stations for US$2.6 billion (A$2.9 billion) to <a href="/wiki/Vitol" title="Vitol">Vitol</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>-based company.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Vitol stated that the Geelong refinery will remain open, as the company plans to expand further into the Australian market. At the time of the sale, Royal Dutch Shell was expected to continue investment into the Australian market, with projects that involve Chevron Corp., <a href="/wiki/Woodside_Petroleum" title="Woodside Petroleum">Woodside Petroleum</a> and Prelude.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloom_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloom-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shell sold 9.5% of its 23.1% stake in <a href="/wiki/Woodside_Petroleum" title="Woodside Petroleum">Woodside Petroleum</a> in June 2014 and advised that it had reached an agreement for Woodside to buy back 9.5% of its shares at a later stage. Shell became a major shareholder in Woodside after a 2001 takeover attempt was blocked by then federal Treasurer <a href="/wiki/Peter_Costello" title="Peter Costello">Peter Costello</a> and the corporation has been open about its intention to sell its stake in Woodside as part of its target to shed assets. At a general body meeting, held on 1 August 2014, 72 percent of shareholders voted to approve the buy-back, short of the 75 percent vote that was required for approval. A statement from Shell read: "Royal Dutch Shell acknowledges the outcome of Woodside Petroleum Limited\'s shareholders\' negative vote on the selective buy-back proposal. Shell is reviewing its options in relation to its remaining 13.6 percent holding."<sup id="cite_ref-ShellWoodside_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShellWoodside-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_energy">Alternative energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Alternative energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In the early 2000s Shell moved into <a href="/wiki/Alternative_energy" title="Alternative energy">alternative energy</a> and there is now an embryonic "<a href="/wiki/Renewables" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewables">Renewables</a>" business that has made investments in <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>. The forestry business went the way of nuclear, coal, metals and electricity generation, and was disposed of in 2003. In 2006 Shell paid <a href="/wiki/SolarWorld" title="SolarWorld">SolarWorld</a> to take over its entire solar business<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> and in 2008, the company withdrew from the <a href="/wiki/London_Array" title="London Array">London Array</a> which has become the world\'s largest offshore wind farm.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shell also is involved in large-scale hydrogen projects. HydrogenForecast.com describes Shell\'s approach thus far as consisting of "baby steps", but with an underlying message of "extreme optimism".<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shell holds 50% of <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%ADzen" title="Ra\xc3\xadzen">Ra\xc3\xadzen</a>, a joint venture with Brazilian sugarcane producer <a href="/wiki/Cosan" title="Cosan">Cosan</a> which is the third-largest Brazil-based energy company by revenues and a major producer of <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sugarcane_Ethanol_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sugarcane_Ethanol-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2016, Shell won the auction for the 700 MW <a href="/wiki/Borssele#Energy" title="Borssele">Borssele III &amp; IV</a> <a href="/wiki/Offshore_wind_farm" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore wind farm">offshore wind farms</a> at a price of 5.45 <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">c</a>/kWh, beating 6 other <a href="/wiki/Consortium" title="Consortium">consortia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2017, Shell\'s CEO Ben van Beurden announced Shell\'s plan to cut half of its carbon emissions by 2050, and 20 percent by 2035. In this regard, Shell promised to spend $2 billion annually on renewable energy sources. Shell began to develop its wind energy segment in 2001, the company now operates six wind farms in the United States and is part of a plan to build two offshore wind farms in the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_projects">Current projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Current projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arctic">Arctic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Arctic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Following the purchase of an offshore lease in 2005, Shell initiated its US$4.5&#160;billion <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> drilling program in 2006, after the corporation purchased the "<a href="/wiki/Kulluk" title="Kulluk">Kulluk</a>" oil rig and leased the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Noble_Discoverer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Noble Discoverer (page does not exist)">Noble Discoverer</a> drillship.<sup id="cite_ref-offshore170306_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-offshore170306-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-petroleum040207_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-petroleum040207-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> At inception, the project was led by Pete Slaiby, a Shell executive who had previously worked in the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jon_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jon-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> However, after the purchase of a second offshore lease in 2008, Shell only commenced drilling work in 2012, due to the refurbishment of rigs, permit delays from the relevant authorities and lawsuits.<sup id="cite_ref-ng270712_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ng270712-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-adn270612_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adn270612-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jerry_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jerry-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The plans to drill in the Arctic led to protests from environmental groups, particularly <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a>; furthermore, analysts in the energy field, as well as related industries, also expressed skepticism due to perceptions that drilling in the region is "too dangerous because of harsh conditions and remote locations".<sup id="cite_ref-Jerry_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jerry-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Phil_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Phil-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Further problems hampered the Arctic project after the commencement of drilling in 2012, as Shell dealt with a series of issues that involved air permits, Coast Guard certification of a marine vessel and severe damage to essential oil-spill equipment. Additionally, difficult weather conditions resulted in the delay of drilling during mid-2012 and the already dire situation was exacerbated by the "Kulluk" incident at the end of the year. Royal Dutch Shell had invested nearly US$5 billion by this stage of the project.<sup id="cite_ref-Jon_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jon-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jerry_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jerry-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As the <i>Kulluk</i> oil rig was being towed to the American state of <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a> to be serviced in preparation for the 2013 drilling season, a winter storm on 27 December 2012 caused the towing crews, as well as the rescue service, to lose control of the situation. As of 1 January 2013, the Kulluk was grounded off the coast Sitkalidak Island, near the eastern end of Kodiak Island. Following the accident, a <i>Fortune</i> magazine contacted Larry McKinney, the executive director at the Harte Research Institute for Gulf of Mexico Studies at Texas A&amp;M, and he explained that "A two-month delay in the Arctic is not a two-month delay ... A two-month delay could wipe out the entire drilling season."<sup id="cite_ref-Jon_112-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jon-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It was unclear if Shell would recommence drilling in mid-2013, following the "Kulluk" incident and, in February 2013, the corporation stated that it would "pause" its closely watched drilling project off the Alaskan coast in 2013, and will instead prepare for future exploration.<sup id="cite_ref-Mat_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mat-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> In January 2014, the corporation announced the extension of the suspension of its drilling program in the Arctic, with chief executive van Beurden explaining that the project is "under review" due to both market and internal issues.<sup id="cite_ref-Terry_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Terry-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A June 2014 interview with Pickard indicated that, following a forensic analysis of the problems encountered in 2012, Royal Dutch Shell will continue with the project and Pickard stated that she perceives the future of the corporation activity in the Arctic region as a long-term "marathon".<sup id="cite_ref-Ann_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ann-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Pickard stated that the forensic "look back" revealed "there was an on/off switch" and further explained:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>\nIn other words, don\'t spend the money unless you\'re sure you\'re going to have the legal environment to go forward. Don\'t spend the money unless you\'re sure you\'re going to have the permit. No, I can\'t tell you that I\'m going to have that permit until June, but we need to plan like we\'re going to have that permit in June. And so probably the biggest lesson is to make sure we could smooth out the on/off switches wherever we could and take control of our own destiny.<sup id="cite_ref-Ann_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ann-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>Based upon the interview with Pickard, Shell is approaching the project as an investment that will reap energy resources with a lifespan of around 30 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Ann_60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ann-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ShellgebouwAmsterdam.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/ShellgebouwAmsterdam.JPG/170px-ShellgebouwAmsterdam.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/ShellgebouwAmsterdam.JPG/255px-ShellgebouwAmsterdam.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/ShellgebouwAmsterdam.JPG/340px-ShellgebouwAmsterdam.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ShellgebouwAmsterdam.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former Shell Research and Technology Centre, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brent_Spar_platform">Brent Spar platform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Brent Spar platform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the 1990s, protesters criticised the company\'s environmental record, particularly the possible pollution caused by the proposed disposal of the <a href="/wiki/Brent_Spar" title="Brent Spar">Brent Spar</a> platform into the North Sea. Despite support from the UK government, Shell reversed the decision under public pressure but maintained that sinking the platform would have been environmentally better.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Shell subsequently published an unequivocal commitment to <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a>, supported by executive speeches reinforcing this commitment.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2004_overstatement_of_oil_reserves">2004 overstatement of oil reserves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: 2004 overstatement of oil reserves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2004 Shell overstated its oil reserves, resulting in loss of confidence in the group, a \xc2\xa317&#160;million fine by the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Services_Authority" title="Financial Services Authority">Financial Services Authority</a> and the departure of the chairman <a href="/wiki/Philip_Watts" title="Philip Watts">Philip Watts</a>. A lawsuit resulted in the payment of $450&#160;million to non-American shareholders in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_communications">Corporate communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Corporate communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shell_Centre,_London,_UK,_June_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Shell_Centre%2C_London%2C_UK%2C_June_2004.jpg/170px-Shell_Centre%2C_London%2C_UK%2C_June_2004.jpg" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Shell_Centre%2C_London%2C_UK%2C_June_2004.jpg/255px-Shell_Centre%2C_London%2C_UK%2C_June_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Shell_Centre%2C_London%2C_UK%2C_June_2004.jpg/340px-Shell_Centre%2C_London%2C_UK%2C_June_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="423" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shell_Centre,_London,_UK,_June_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Shell_Centre" title="Shell Centre">Shell Centre</a> building in London, UK</div></div></div>\n<p>Shell\'s advertising regarding its <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> business has been described as a <a href="/wiki/Greenwash" class="mw-redirect" title="Greenwash">greenwash</a> by some environmental lobbies,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> leading to criticism from the British <a href="/wiki/Advertising_Standards_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Advertising Standards Authority (United Kingdom)">Advertising Standards Authority</a> which ruled that Shell had misled the public in an advertisement when it claimed that a $10&#160;billion oil sands project in Alberta, Canada was a "sustainable energy source".<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_and_safety">Health and safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Health and safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A number of incidents over the years led to criticism of Shell\'s <a href="/wiki/Health_and_safety" class="mw-redirect" title="Health and safety">health and safety</a> record, including repeated warnings by the UK Health and Safety Executive about the poor state of the company\'s North Sea platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the beginning of 1996, several human rights groups <a href="/wiki/Ken_Saro-Wiwa#Family_lawsuits_against_Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Ken Saro-Wiwa">brought cases to hold Shell accountable</a> for alleged human rights violations in Nigeria, including summary execution, crimes against humanity, torture, inhumane treatment and arbitrary arrest and detention. In particular, Shell stood accused of collaborating in the execution of <a href="/wiki/Ken_Saro-Wiwa" title="Ken Saro-Wiwa">Ken Saro-Wiwa</a> and eight other leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Ogoni_people" title="Ogoni people">Ogoni</a> tribe of southern Nigeria, who were hanged in 1995 by Nigeria\'s then military rulers.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> The lawsuits were brought against Royal Dutch Shell and Brian Anderson, the head of its Nigerian operation.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, Shell agreed to pay $15.5m in a legal settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Shell has not accepted any liability over the allegations against it.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2009, Shell was the subject of an Amnesty International report into the deterioration of human rights as a consequence of Shell\'s activities in the <a href="/wiki/Niger_Delta" title="Niger Delta">Niger Delta</a>. In particular, Amnesty criticised the continuation of <a href="/wiki/Gas_flaring" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas flaring">gas flaring</a> and Shell\'s slow response to oil spills.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In 1998, on its first public report on community and environmental issues in Nigeria, Shell promised "to end the practice of gas flaring in ten years, while pledging to establish a youth training scheme in Ogoniland".<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010, a leaked cable revealed that Shell claims to have inserted staff into all the main ministries of the Nigerian government and know "everything that was being done in those ministries", according to Shell\'s top executive in Nigeria. The same executive also boasted that the Nigerian government had forgotten about the extent of Shell\'s infiltration.<sup id="cite_ref-grip_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grip-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Documents released in 2009 (but not used in the court case) reveal that Shell regularly made payments to the Nigerian military in order to prevent protests.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_paid_nigerian_military_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_paid_nigerian_military-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arctic_project">Arctic project</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Arctic project">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to the Bureau of Ocean Energy Management report in 2015 the chances of a major spill in a deep-sea Arctic drilling is 75% before century\'s end.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kodiak">Kodiak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Kodiak">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 2010 Greenpeace activists painted "No Arctic Drilling" with spilled BP oil on the side of a ship in the Gulf of Mexico that was en route to explore for Arctic oil for Shell. At the protest, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Radford" title="Phil Radford">Phil Radford</a> of Greenpeace called for "President Obama [to] ban all offshore oil drilling and call for an end to the use of oil in our cars by 2030."<sup id="cite_ref-Phil_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Phil-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 16 March 2012, 52 Greenpeace activists from five different countries boarded <i><a href="/wiki/MSV_Fennica" title="MSV Fennica">Fennica</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/MSV_Nordica" title="MSV Nordica">Nordica</a></i>, multipurpose <a href="/wiki/Icebreaker" title="Icebreaker">icebreakers</a> chartered to support Shell\'s drilling rigs near Alaska.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Around the same time period, a reporter for <i>Fortune</i> magazine spoke with Edward Itta, an Inupiat Eskimo leader and the former mayor of the North Slope Borough, who expressed that he was conflicted about Shell\'s plans in the Arctic, as he was very concerned that an oil spill could destroy the Inupiat Eskimo\'s hunting-and-fishing culture, but his borough also received major tax revenue from oil and gas production; additionally, further revenue from energy activity was considered crucial to the future of the living standard in Itta\'s community.<sup id="cite_ref-Jon_112-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jon-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2012, Greenpeace activists shut down 53&#160;Shell petrol stations in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> and <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> in a protest against the company\'s plans to drill for oil in the Arctic. Greenpeace\'s "<a href="/wiki/Save_the_Arctic" title="Save the Arctic">Save the Arctic</a>" campaign aims to prevent oil drilling and industrial fishing in the Arctic by declaring the uninhabited area around the North Pole a global sanctuary.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A review was announced after the <i>Kulluk</i> oil rig ran aground near Kodiak Island in December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-ap080113_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ap080113-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In response, Shell filed lawsuits to seek injunctions from possible protests, and <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Jealous" class="mw-redirect" title="Benjamin Jealous">Benjamin Jealous</a> of the <a href="/wiki/NAACP" title="NAACP">NAACP</a> and Radford argued that the legal action was "trampling Americans\' rights."<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> According to Greenpeace, Shell lodged a request with Google to take down video footage of a Greenpeace protest action that occurred at the Shell-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> (F1) Belgian Grand Prix on 25 August 2013, in which "SaveTheArctic.org" banners appear at the winners\' podium ceremony. In the video, the banners rise up automatically\xe2\x80\x94activists controlled their appearance with the use of four radio car antennas\xe2\x80\x94revealing the website URL, alongside an image that consists of half of a polar bear\'s head and half of the Shell logo.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Royal Dutch Shell then announced a "pause" in the timeline of the project in early 2013<sup id="cite_ref-Mat_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mat-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> and, in September 2015, the corporation announced the extension of the suspension of its drilling program in the Arctic.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Polar_Pioneer">Polar Pioneer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Polar Pioneer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>A June 2014 interview with the corporation\'s new executive vice president of the Arctic indicated that Royal Dutch Shell will continue with its activity in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Ann_60-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ann-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Terry_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Terry-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Arctic_drilling_protests" title="Seattle Arctic drilling protests">protests began in May 2015</a> in response to the news that the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Seattle" title="Port of Seattle">Port of Seattle</a> made an agreement with Shell to berth  rigs at the Port\'s Terminal 5 during the off-season of <a href="/wiki/Oil_exploration" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil exploration">oil exploration</a> in <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaskan</a> waters. The arrival of Shell\'s new Arctic drilling vessel, <i>Polar Pioneer</i> (<a href="/wiki/IMO_number" title="IMO number">IMO number</a>:&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.marinetraffic.com/ais/details/ships/imo:8754140">8754140</a>), a <a href="/wiki/Semi-submersible" title="Semi-submersible">semi-submersible</a> <a href="/wiki/Offshore_drilling" title="Offshore drilling">offshore drilling</a> rig, was greeted by large numbers of environmental protesters paddling kayaks in <a href="/wiki/Elliott_Bay" title="Elliott Bay">Elliott Bay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Beekman2015a_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beekman2015a-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC2015_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2015-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 May 2015 it was reported that during a coast guard inspection of <i>Polar Pioneer</i>, a piece of anti-pollution gear failed, resulting in fines and delay of the operation.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Oil executives from Total and Eni interviewed by the <i>New York Times</i>, expressed scepticism about Shell\'s new ambitions for offshore drilling in the Arctic, and cited economic and environmental hurdles. ConocoPhillips and Statoil suspended Arctic drilling earlier, after Shell\'s failed attempt in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_spills">Oil spills</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Oil spills">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ul><li>Shell was responsible for around 21,000 gallons of oil spilled near <a href="/wiki/Tracy,_California" title="Tracy, California">Tracy, California</a> in May 2016 due to a pipeline crack.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Shell was responsible for a 88,200-gallon oil spill in the Gulf of Mexico in May 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Two ruptures in a Shell Oil Co. pipeline in Altamont, California - one in September 2015 and another in May 2016 - had some questioning whether the Office of the State Fire Marshal, charged with overseeing the pipeline, was doing an adequate job.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paradise_Papers">Paradise Papers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Paradise Papers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 5 November 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Paradise_Papers" title="Paradise Papers">Paradise Papers</a>, a set of confidential <a href="/wiki/Electronic_document" title="Electronic document">electronic documents</a> relating to <a href="/wiki/Offshore_investment" title="Offshore investment">offshore investment</a>, revealed that Argentine Energy Minister <a href="/wiki/Juan_Jos%C3%A9_Aranguren" title="Juan Jos\xc3\xa9 Aranguren">Juan Jos\xc3\xa9 Aranguren</a> was revealed to have managed the <a href="/wiki/Offshore_companies" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore companies">offshore companies</a> \'Shell Western Supply and Trading Limited\' and \'Sol Antilles y Guianas Limited\', both subsidiaries of Shell. One is the main bidder for the purchase of diesel oil by the current government through the state owned CAMMESA (Compa\xc3\xb1\xc3\xada Administradora del Mercado Mayorista El\xc3\xa9ctrico).<sup id="cite_ref-perfil1_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perfil1-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nigeria_corruption_scandals">Nigeria corruption scandals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Nigeria corruption scandals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Royal Dutch Shell and Italy\'s <a href="/wiki/Eni" title="Eni">Eni</a> will stand trial in Italy over allegations of corruption in the 2011 purchase of a <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Nigeria" title="Petroleum industry in Nigeria">big offshore oil field</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> known as OPL 245. Shell and Eni reportedly paid $1.3 billion in bribes.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> According to Barnaby Pace of campaign group <a href="/wiki/Global_Witness" title="Global Witness">Global Witness</a>, "This trial should be a wake-up call to the oil industry. Some of the most senior executives at two of the biggest companies in the world could face prison sentences for a deal that was struck under their watch."<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>In March 2018, Royal Dutch Shell has filed a criminal complaint against Peter Robinson, a former vice president for sub-Saharan Africa. Shell said the two cases were unrelated.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Dutch_Shell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: See
